тАШ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдп’ рдЗрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдорд╖реНрдЯрд╛рджрд╢рдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рднреГрдЧреБрдЧреЛрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рд╡реЗрдирд╕реНрдпрд╛рд░реНрд╖рдВ рдкрд╡рдорд╛рдирд╕реЛрдорджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рдХрдореН ред рдПрдХрд╛рджрд╢реАрджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢реНрдпреМ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрднреМ рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╛ рдЬрдЧрддреНрдпрдГ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪрд╛рдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдореН-’ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдп рджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢ рд╡реЗрдиреЛ рднрд╛рд░реНрдЧрд╡реЛ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдмрдиреНрддрдореН’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЧрддреЛ рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧрдГ рее

Jamison Brereton

85 (797)
Soma Pavama╠Дna
Vena Bh─Бrgava
12 verses: jagat─л, except triс╣гс╣нubh 11тАУ12
The last two hymns of the jagat─л group, IX.85тАУ86, break the standard pattern of decreasing numbers of verses, having twelve and forty-eight verses respectively, after a group of hymns with five verses (IX.75тАУ84). However, each of these longer hymns can be divided into a series of shorter ones, which then conform to the patterns of hymn arrangement. In the case of IX.85, it consists of three groups of four verses each. The entire assemblage is attributed to Vena Bh─Бrgava, also the supposed poet of the enigmatic тАЬVenaтАЭ hymn (X.123; see also a brief discussion under IX.83). As we will see, there are certainly striking similarities between the last quartet of IX.85 (vss. 9тАУ12) and X.123.
The first quartet (vss. 1тАУ4) begins with Soma the militant, keeping unworthy and hostile forces at bay and aiding Indra in the same enterprise (vss. 1тАУ2). His relation ship to Indra persists in verses 3тАУ4, which show a more positive side of the militant Soma: his status as king (vs. 3) and winner of space for us (vs. 4).
The second section (vss. 5тАУ8) is quite straightforward and focuses on the purifi cation of the soma, deploying the standard tropes.
As noted the final four verses (9тАУ12) strongly resemble the Vena hymn (X.123), but they are considerably easier to decode. They concern heavenly Soma, who is identified with the sun, but who also appears in a number of different guises: a bull, a poet, and a king (all in vs. 9), an ox (vs. 10), an eagle, a child, and a bird (vs. 11), and finally a Gandharva (vs. 12).

Jamison Brereton Notes

For the four-vs. sequences and their contents, see published introduction.

068-086 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

The trimeter portion of the IXth Maс╣Зс╕Нala begins with IX.68, and the Jagat─л section goes through IX.86.

85-86 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

On the structure of the last two hymns of the Jagat─л group, see the published

introductions to IX.85 and 86. In brief, after a series of hymns of 5 vss. (IX.75-84), these last two have 12 vss. and 48 vss. respectively. However, they are clearly composites: IX.85 consists of three groups of four vss. apiece, IX.86 of 16 tс╣Ыcas. The standard principles of hymn arrangement can thus be restored.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬFlow forth, Soma, well-effused for Indra; may disease and the r─Бkс╣гasas be (kept) far off; let not the double-dealers be exhilarated by your juices; may the Soma-juices be full of wealth at this (sacrifice).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O Soma, when well pressed, flow around for Indra. Let affliction be gone, along with demonic power.
Let the duplicitous not reach the exhilaration of your sap: let the
wealth-bringing drops be here.

Griffith

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPurified (Soma), animate us in battle; for you are powerful, dear to the gods, the exhilarator. Slay our foes, approach (us) who desire (to propitiate you by) praises; Indra, drink the Soma, destroy our adversaries.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Spur us on in the clash, self-purifying one, for you are the skill of the gods, their dear exhilarating drink.
Smash the rivals; (come) here to those seeking blessings. Drink the soma, Indra; smash down the scorners for us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In p─Бda c the preverbs abhy ─Б╠Бare oddly positioned, after the caesura, and, more important, the two apparent acc. objects ┼Ы├бtr┼лn тАШrivalsтАЩ and bhandan─Бy├бtaс╕е тАШthose seeking blessingsтАЩ are antithetical, with only the first an appropriate obj. to jah├н. The problems disappear if, with Geldner, we supply a second verb to go with the preverbs and to govern the 2nd acc. A verb of motion fits well, and тИЪi, тИЪgam, and тИЪy─Б all appear with this combination of preverbs, whereas тИЪhan does not. Geldner goes for slightly richer semantics: тАЬ(komm) тАж zu (Hilfe)тАЭ - without specifying what verb he supplies, but note that тИЪav does not appear with those preverbs.

The identities of Soma and Indra appear to bleed into each other in the course of the vs. In ab the 2nd ps. subject is clearly Soma, on the basis of voc. pavam─Бna (a) and priy├│ m├бdaс╕е (b). The assumption then is that the impv. jah├н in c is also addressed to Soma. But in d we get direct address of Indra and at the end of the p─Бda he is the subj. of a second jahi. Therefore p─Бda c, which contains no lexical clue to the addressee, could be addressed either to Soma or to Indra (or both).

Griffith

O Pavamana, urge us forward in the fight thou art the vigour of the Gods, the well-loved drink.
Smite thou our enemies who raise the shout of joy: Indra, drink Soma juice, and drive away our foes.

Geldner

Mach uns im Wettkampf scharf, o Pavamana, denn du bist die Kraft der G├╢tter, ihr lieber Rauschtrank! Erschlage die Feinde, komm denen zu Hilfe, die l├╢bliches erstreben! Trink, Indra, den Soma, drisch auf unsere Ver├дchter los!

Grassmann

Gib Muth und Kraft uns in der Schlacht, o flammender; denn du bist Kraft der G├╢tter, du ihr Heber Trank; Die Feinde t├╢dte, die nach Gut begierig sind, Trink Soma, Indra, jage unsre Hasser fort.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou flow, Indu, the inviolable, the most exhilarating; you are yourself the best support for Indra; may sages approach and glorify you the ruler of this world.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The best support: food

Jamison Brereton

Undeceivable, you purify yourself as most exhilarating, o drop; you become the very self of Indra, the highest wellspring.
Many men of inspired thought cry out to him; they seek out the king of this creation.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The blending of identities in 2cd is made explicit in p─Бda b here, where Soma is called тАЬthe very self of IndraтАЭ (─Бtm├йndrasya).

On the meaning of the secondary root тИЪniс╣Гs see comm. ad VIII.43.10. There I stated my preference for maintaining the older gloss тАШkissтАЩ, against the colorless тАШseek outтАЩ, which was suggested by Got┼Н and adopted by EWA, etc. However, I must admit that, at least superficially, тАШseek outтАЩ works better here than тАШkissтАЩ and it is reflected in the published translation But a ceremonial kiss signaling fealty is certainly possible - like kissing the popeтАЩs ring or the widespread custom of kissing someoneтАЩs feet as a gesture of respect. So Ober (I.531-32) тАЬSie k├╝ssen den [Fuss des] K├╢nig[s] dieser Erde.тАЭ Both Geldner and Renou render the phrase without interposing a bodypart, e.g., тАЬils baisent le roi de ce monde.тАЭ I am now inclined towards the more precise and physical тАЬthey kiss the king,тАЭ rather than the published translationтАЩs тАЬThey seek out the king.тАЭ This interpr.

is made the more likely because тАЬkissingтАЭ Soma in the ritual can well indicate consuming soma by mouth, that is, drinking it.

Griffith

Unharmed, best Cheerer, thou, O Indu, flowest on: thou, even thou thyself, art Indra’s noblest food.
Full many a wise man lifts to thee the song of praise, and hails thee with a kiss as Sovran of this world.

Geldner

Unbeirrt l├дuterst du dich, o Saft, als der Berauschendste. Du bist Indra┬┤s Leben, seine h├╢chste Labung. Viele Nachsinnende stimmen in den Gesang ein; sie ber├╝hren den K├╢nig dieser Welt mit dem Munde.

Grassmann

Du rieselst lauter, Indu, o berauschendster, des Indra Hauch und beste Labung bist du ja; Dir stimmen viele S├дnger ihre Lieder an, begr├╝ssen freudig dich als K├╢nig dieser Welt.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe guide of thousands, flowing in a hundred streams, marvellous, Indu flows forth for Indra, (his) beloved beverage; approach (the filter) winning (us) land, winning water, O Soma, sprinkler, make our path broad.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Having a thousand channels and a hundred streams, unerring, the drop, the desirable honey purifies itself for Indra.
Winning a dwelling place, winning the waters, rush onward. Make a wide course for us, o Soma the rewarder.

Griffith

Wondrous, with hundred streams, hymned in a thousand songs, Indu pours out for Indra his delightrul meath.
Winning us land and waters, flow thou hitherward: Rainer of bounties, Soma, make broad way for us.

Geldner

рд╣реЗ рд╕реЛрдо рдХрдирд┐рдХреНрд░рджрддреН рд╢рдмреНрджрдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреН рдХрд▓рд╢реЗ рд╡рд░реНрддрдорд╛рдирдГ рдЧреЛрднрд┐рдГ рдкрдпреЛрднрд┐рдГ рдЕрдЬреНрдпрд╕реЗ рд╕рд┐рдХреНрддреЛ рднрд╡рд╕рд┐ ред рдЕрд╡реНрдпрдпрдореН рдЕрд╡рд┐рдордпрдВ рд╡рд╛рд░рдВ рд╡рд╛рд▓рдВ рджрд╢рд╛рдкрд╡рд┐рддреНрд░рдВ рд╕рдордпрд╛ рддрддреНрд╕рдореАрдкреЗ рд╡рд┐ рдЕрд░реНрд╖рд╕рд┐ рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдзрдВ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрд╕рд┐ ред рдорд░реНрдореГрдЬреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдГ рд╢реЛрдзреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдГ рдЕрддреНрдпреЛ рди рдЕрд╢реНрд╡ рдЗрд╡ рд╕рд╛рдирд╕рд┐рдГ рд╕рдВрднрдЬрдирд╢реАрд▓рд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рд╣реЗ рд╕реЛрдо рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рдЬрдард░реЗ рд╕рдордХреНрд╖рд░рдГ рд╕рдореНрдпрдХреН рдХреНрд╖рд░рд╕рд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬCrying aloud you are blended in the pitcher with curds and milk, you pass through the woollen fleece in the midst; being cleansed like a horse, distributing (gifts), you flow, Soma, into Indra’s belly.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Ever roaring, you are anointed [/driven] with cows in(to) the tub. You rush across the sheepтАЩs fleece all at once.
Constantly being groomed like a winning steed, Soma, you have flowed entirely into the belly of Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The passive ajyase has, as often in this maс╣Зс╕Нala, a double meaning, тАШis anointedтАЩ (тИЪa├▒j) and тАШis drivenтАЩ (тИЪaj).

On the meaning (тАШall at onceтАЩ, not тАШin the middleтАЩ) and the formulaic construction of sam├бy─Б, see comm. ad I.113.10.

Griffith

Roaring within the beaker thou art balmed with milk: thou passest through the fleecy filter all at once.
Carefully cleansed and decked like a prizewinning steed, O Soma, thou hast flowed down within Indra’s throat.

Geldner

Br├╝llend wirst du in dem Kruge mit Milch gesalbt; du rinnst mitten durch das Schafhaar. Wie ein gewinnendes Rennpferd geputzt, bist du, Soma, in Indra┬┤s Bauch geflossen.

Grassmann

Mit Milch der Kuh wirst wiehernd du im Krug gesalbt und mitten durch die Widderwolle str├╢mest du; Gestriegelt wie ein Renner, der den Preis erstrebt, bist, Soma, du geflossen in des Indra Bauch.

Elizarenkova

Flow onward sweet of flavour for the Heavenly Race, for Indra sweet, whose name is easily invoked:
Flow sweet for Mitra, Varuna, and Vayu, rich in meath, inviolable for Brhaspati.

English translation:

тАЬThe ten fingers clean the horse in the pitcher; among the vipras the worshippers send forth praises; the filtered (juices) hasten to the fair praise, the exhilarating Soma juices enter Indra.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The ten fingers groom the steed in the tub. The thoughts, the words of the inspired poets press forward.
Purifying themselves, they rush to the lovely praise hymn. The
exhilarating drops enter Indra. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бdas 7c and 8a have almost identical structure: p├бvam─Бn─Б abhy ├аrс╣гanti su(с╣гс╣нut├нm) p├бvam─Бno abhy ├аrс╣г─Б su(v─л╠Бryam) which effects the transition from 3rd pl. to 2nd sg.

Griffith

Ten rapid fingers deck the Courser in the jar: with hymns the holy singers send their voices forth.
The filtering juices hasten to their eulogy, the drops that gladden find their way to Indra’s heart.

Geldner

Die zehn Finger putzen den Renner in dem Kruge; die Gedanken und Worte der Redekundigen kommen hervor. Sich l├дuternd str├╢men sie dem Loblied zu; die berauschenden S├дfte gehen in Indra ein.

Grassmann

Zehn Finger striegeln in dem Krug das schnelle Ross; der S├дnger Lieder und Gebete dringen vor; Dem Lobgesang entgegen gehn die rieselnden, in Indra’s Bauch die Indu’s, die berauschenden.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Soma), when filtered, bring us male progeny, extensive pastures, a large and spacious mansion; let no hinderer of this (rite) be lord over us; Indu, through you may we win all wealth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Purifying yourself, rush to an abundance of heroes, to wide pasturage, to great, extensive shelter.
Let no constricting pressure take control of this (soma) of ours. O
drop, with you may we win prize after prize.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The somewhat awkward tr. тАЬconstricting pressureтАЭ reflects the literal, additive sense of p├бriс╣г┼лti-: p├бri тАШaroundтАЩ + тИЪs┼л тАШimpel, thrustтАЩ. Maybe something like тАЬsqueezingтАЭ would sound a bit more idiomatic, though it is hard to find any English idiom that more or less represents the etymology and fits with the verb. Of course, narrowness and constriction are particularly feared and avoided in the Rig Veda. Perhaps тАЬclaustrophobiaтАЭ might work, though of course the -phobia part is absent; тАЬconstrictionтАЭ is probably the best choice in English. It is also not clear what threat p├бriс╣г┼лti- poses to the ritual soma, which, after all, has been subjected to serious pressing (via the phonologically similar but unrelated root тИЪsu) and therefore has nothing left to fear in that regard. In real world terms it of course refers to the opposite of the тАЬwide pasturage and great, extensive shelterтАЭ that Soma is urged to rush to in p─Бda b. In this regard it is similar to the words aс╣Гhat├н-, ├бс╣Гhas- тАШconstriction, constraintтАЩ. The other occurrence of p├бriс╣г┼лti- (I.119.6) is found in a similar context, with a contrast between constraint and wide space: yuv├бс╣Г rebh├бm p├бriс╣г┼лter uruс╣гyathaс╕е. JPB tr. тАЬYou give Rebha space from being besieged,тАЭ but in my opinion the sense is more particular: тАЬyou give Rebha wide space from (/out of) constriction.тАЭ On ─л┼Ыata see comm. ad I.23.9.

While thou art purified pour on us hero strength, great, far-extended shelter, spacious pasturage.
Let no oppression master this our holy work: may we, O Indu, gain all opulence through thee.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe showerer, the beholder, has taken his station upon heaven, the seer has illumined the luminaries of heaven; the king passes through the filter with a shout, (the Soma juices) the beholders of men milk forth the ambrosia of heaven.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The wide-gazing bull has mounted heaven. The poet has caused the luminous realms of heaven to shine forth.
The king goes ever bellowing across the filter. Those having the eyes of men milk for themselves the beestings of heaven.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The double vision of both heavenly Soma/Sun and earthly ritual soma is clear here, with p─Бdas a, b, d all having a celestial orientation, each containing a form of div-/dyu- тАШheavenтАЩ, while the filter of p─Бda c brings us back to the ritual. The subj.

of d is probably, on the one hand, the ritual officiants, who perform the ritual action of milking (that is, pressing) the soma. But the substance obtained is тАЬthe beestings [colostrum, first milk] of heavenтАЭ (p─лy├║с╣гam тАж div├бс╕е), and the next vs. makes clear that those performing the milking here are also the ven─Б╠Бс╕е тАШseekersтАЩ in 10b, where they are located тАЬin the vault of heavenтАЭ (div├│ n─Б╠Бke).

09-12 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, these four vss. treat the identification of Soma and the sun and are similar to the very enigmatic Vena hymn, X.123, which is attributed to the same poet, Vena Bh─Бrgava.

Griffith

The Steer who sees afar hath risen above the sky: the Sage hath caused the lights of heaven to give their shine.
The. King is passing through the filter with a roar: they drain the milk of heaven from him who looks on men.

Geldner

Der Bulle hat den Himmel erstiegen, weitschauend; der Seher hat die Leuchten des Himmels erleuchtet. Der K├╢nig geht br├╝llend ├╝ber die Seihe; die mit dem Herrenauge melken den Rahm des Himmels.

Grassmann

Zum Himmel stieg weitschauend jetzt der Stier empor, der weise hat das Licht des Himmels angesteckt; Der K├╢nig schreitet durch die Seihe br├╝llend hin, des M├дnner schaunden Himmels Milchtrunk melkt er sich.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIn the heaven of the bright (ssacrifice) the sweet-voiced Venas severally milk forth the sprinkler, the mountain-haunting (Soma); (they sprinkle him) nourished in the waters, juicy, in the ocean (-like pitcher), in the wave of the river; (they sprinkle him) sweet-flavoured, in the filter.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

In the heaven: n─Бke = free from pain, the plural ce called havirdh─Бna;

Divaс╕е = dyotam─Бnasya yaj├▒asya

Jamison Brereton

In the vault of heaven the seekers milk honey-tongued, inexhaustible (streams) from the mountain-dwelling ox,
the droplet growing strong in the waters, in the sea, the honeyed one in the wave of the river, in the filter.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The cosmic/natural and the earthly/ritual double vision is played out simultaneously throughout this vs. In ab the seekers milk the streams тАЬin the vault of heavenтАЭ (div├│ n─Б╠Бke) but milk them out of тАЬthe mountain-dwelling oxтАЭ (ukс╣г├бс╣Зaс╣Г giristh─Б╠Бm), the earthly soma plant. In c the drop grows strong not only тАЬin the watersтАЭ (aps├║), presumably the ritual waters used to swell the plant, but also тАЬin the seaтАЭ (samudr├б ─Б╠Б); in d it is both тАЬin the wave of the riverтАЭ (s├нndhor ┼лrm─Б╠Б) and тАЬin the filterтАЭ (pav├нtra ─Б╠Б).

On the basis of the shared verb (duhate in 9d, duhanti in 10b) the ven─Б╠Бс╕е here appear to be identical to the subjects of 9d, as suggested above.

P─Бda b is identical to IX.73.4. As noted in the comm. thereon, there is good reason to supply тАЬstreamsтАЭ (dh─Б╠Бr─Бс╕е) as the referent for the pl. adjs. m├бdhujihv─Б(с╕е) and asa┼Ыc├бtaс╕е, which are therefore fem. acc. pl. Curiously Geldner takes the former as nom. pl. m. here, though fem. in 73.4, while Ober (II.13149-50, ) takes them both as nom. pl. m.; Renou tr. as I do.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, these four vss. treat the identification of Soma and the sun and are similar to the very enigmatic Vena hymn, X.123, which is attributed to the same poet, Vena Bh─Бrgava.

The two tr. of ven├б- in 10b тАШseekersтАЩ and 11b тАШtrackersтАЩ respectively should be harmonized. I would now tr. тАШseekersтАЩ for both.

Griffith

High in the vault of heaven, unceasing, honey-tongued, the Loving Ones drain out the mountain-haunting Steer,-
The drop that hath grown great in waters, in the lake meath-rich, in the stream’s wave and in the cleansing sieve.

Geldner

Auf des Himmels Firmament melken die honigzungigen Seher unversiegliche Str├╢me aus dem bergbewohnenden Stiere, den im Wasser gro├Я gewordenen Tropfen, im Meere, in des Stromes Welle, den s├╝├Яen auf die Seihe.

Grassmann

English translation:

тАЬThe many voices of the Venas praise (the Soma who dwells) in heaven, well-winged, falling (to earth); praises soothe the crying infant, the golden bird, reposing on the earth.тАЭ

The eagle that has flown to the vaultтАФthe many hymns of the trackers yearned after (him).
The thoughts lick the child who always excites wonder, the golden bird standing on the earth.

Griffith

The Loving Ones besought with many voices the Eagle who had flown away to heaven.
Hymns kiss the Youngling worthy of laudation, resting on earth, the Bird of golden colour.

Geldner

Nach dem zum Firmament aufgeflogenen Adler trugen die vielen Reden der Seher Verlangen. Die frommen Gedanken belecken das lautschreiende Junge, den goldenen Vogel, der auf Erden wohnt.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe elevated gandharva abides above the sun contemplating all its forms; the sun shines with white light, radiant he illumines the creative heaven and earth.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

I.e., m─Бtar─Б = nirm─Бtryau; i.e., the two mother; or, the two parents (pitarau)

Jamison Brereton

The Gandharva has stood erect upon the vault, gazing upon all
his forms.
Radiance has flashed forth with blazing blaze; the blazing one has
made the two world-halves, the mothers, shine forth.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This final vs. is esp. close in phraseology to the Vena hymn, with p─Бda a identical to X.123.7a and p─Бda c almost identical to X.123.8c. Note also that ├бdhi n─Б╠Бke asth─Бt unites ├бdhi … asth─Бt of our 9a and n─Б╠Бke of our 10a.

Geldner takes the part. pratic├бkс╣г─Бс╣Зaс╕е as transitive/causative тАЬseine Farben alle offenbarendтАЭ (though he questions this in n. 12b); sim. Ober (II.13) тАЬerscheinen lassend.тАЭ RenouтАЩs tr. is like mine (тАЬregardant-en-face toutes les formes siennesтАЭ), although in his n. he considers the opposite possibility, citing passages with pr├бti тИЪcakс╣г that supposedly have this transitive sense. But his exx. are not probative, and the middle voice of the participle makes it esp. unlikely to have this sense.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, these four vss. treat the identification of Soma and the sun and are similar to the very enigmatic Vena hymn, X.123, which is attributed to the same poet, Vena Bh─Бrgava.

Griffith

High to heaven’s vault hath the Gandharva risen, beholding all his varied forms and figures.
His ray hath shone abroad with gleaming splendour: pure, he hath lighted both the worlds, the Parents.

Geldner

Der Gandharva hat sich ├╝ber dem Firmament erhoben, seine Farben alle offenbarend. Sein Strahl ist in heller Glut aufgeleuchtet; er hat die beiden Welten erleuchtet, seine M├╝tter, er der Reine.

Grassmann

Gandharva hat des Himmels H├╢h erstiegen, betrachtend jede Glanzgestalt des Soma’s, Mit hellem Lichte hat sein Glanz gestrahlet, die Welten-Aeltern hat erhellt der lichte.

Elizarenkova

рдЖрд░реНрдпрдореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛, рд░реВрдкрд╛, рдкреНрд░рддрд┐, рдЪрдХреНрд╖рд╛рдгреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдп) рдЕрд╕реНрдп рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдпрдордгреНрдбрд▓рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдиреЗрдХрд╛рдирд┐ рд░реВрдкрд╛рдгрд┐ рдкреНрд░рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдкрдпрдиреН рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ (рдЕрдзрд┐, рдирд╛рдХреЗ, рдЕрд╕реНрдерд╛рддреН) рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЛрдкрд░рд┐ рд╕реБрдЦреЗ рд╡рд┐рд░рд╛рдЬрдорд╛рдиреЛрд╜рд╕реНрддрд┐ред (рдКрд░реНрдзреНрд╡рдГ) рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЛрдкрд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╕реНрддрд┐ (рд╢реБрдХреНрд░реЗрдг) рдирд┐рдЬрдмрд▓реЗрди рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ (рд╢реЛрдЪрд┐рд╖рд╛) рдирд┐рдЬрддреЗрдЬрд╕рд╛ (рднрд╛рдиреБрдГ) рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдпрдордкрд┐ (рд╡рд┐, рдЕрджреНрдпреМрддреН) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдпрддрд┐ред рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ (рд░реЛрджрд╕реА, рдорд╛рддрд░рд╛) рдЕрдиреНрдпрд▓реЛрдХрд▓реЛрдХрд╛рдиреНрддрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рдирд┐рд░реНрдорд╛рддрд╛ (рдкреНрд░рд╛рд░реВрд░реБрдЪрддреН) рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпреЛрдГ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдХреЛрд╜рд╕реНрддрд┐ (рд╢реБрдЪрд┐рдГ) рдкрд╡рд┐рддреНрд░реЛрд╜рд╕реНрддрд┐ред рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ (рдЧрдиреНрдзрд░реНрд╡рдГ) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд▓реЛрдХрд▓реЛрдХрд╛рдиреНрддрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдореН рдЕрдзрд┐рд╖реНрдард╛рддрд╛рд╕реНрддрд┐реерезреирее рдЗрддрд┐ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╛рд╢реАрддрд┐рддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореН рдПрдХрд╛рджрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее
